      <p><b>Mali</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Ë/: primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ÉË/: 'a' in 'father'">ÉË</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Mali.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8a/En-us-Mali.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Mali.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <small>French pronunciation:&nbsp;â</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[mali]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Mali</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">RÃ©publique du Mali</i>; <a href="/wiki/Bambara_language" title="Bambara language">Bambara</a>: <i lang="bm" dir="rtl">ß¡ßßß ßß ßßßßßßß¡ßß£ß</i>, <small>romanized:&nbsp;</small><i lang="bm-Latn" title="Bambara-language romanization">Mali ka Fasojamana</i>, <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula</a>: <i lang="ff-Latn" dir="rtl">ð¤ð¤«ð¤²ð¥ð¤£ð¤¢ð¥ð¤²ð¤£ð¤­ ð¤ð¤¢ð¥ð¤¤ð¤­</i>, <small>romanized:&nbsp;</small><i lang="ff-Latn-Latn" title="Fula-language romanization">Renndaandi Maali</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>. Mali is the eighth-largest country in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, with an area of just over 1,240,000 square kilometres (480,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). The population of Mali is 19.1&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-9">[9]</a></sup> 67% of its population was estimated to be under the age of 25 in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Bamako" title="Bamako">Bamako</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> of Mali consists of eight regions and its borders on the north reach deep into the middle of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara Desert</a>. The country's southern part is in the <a href="/wiki/Sudanian_savanna" title="Sudanian savanna">Sudanian savanna</a>, where the majority of inhabitants live, and both the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">Senegal</a> rivers pass through. The country's economy centres on agriculture and mining. One of Mali's most prominent natural resources is gold, and the country is the third largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> on the African continent.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> It also exports <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Present-day Mali was once part of three West <a href="/wiki/African_empires" title="African empires">African empires</a> that controlled <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">trans-Saharan trade</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Empire" title="Ghana Empire">Ghana Empire</a> (for which <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> is named), the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a> (for which Mali is named), and the <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai Empire</a>. At its peak in 1300, the Mali Empire covered an area about twice the size of modern-day <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and stretched to the west coast of Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In the late 19th century, during the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>, France seized control of Mali, making it a part of <a href="/wiki/French_Sudan" title="French Sudan">French Sudan</a>. French Sudan (then known as the Sudanese Republic) joined with <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> in 1959, achieving independence in 1960 as the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Federation" title="Mali Federation">Mali Federation</a>. Shortly thereafter, following Senegal's withdrawal from the federation, the Sudanese Republic declared itself the independent Republic of Mali. After a long period of one-party rule, a coup in 1991 led to the writing of a new constitution and the establishment of Mali as a democratic, multi-party state. </p>
      <p>In January 2012, an <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mali_conflict_(2012%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Mali conflict (2012âpresent)">armed conflict broke out in northern Mali</a>, in which <a href="/wiki/National_Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Azawad" title="National Movement for the Liberation of Azawad">Tuareg rebels</a> took control of a territory in the north, and in April declared the <a href="/wiki/Secession" title="Secession">secession</a> of a new state, <a href="/wiki/Azawad" title="Azawad">Azawad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The conflict was complicated by a <a href="/wiki/2012_Malian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2012 Malian coup d'Ã©tat">military coup</a> that took place in March<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-15">[15]</a></sup> and later fighting between Tuareg and other rebel factions. In response to territorial gains, the French military launched <a href="/wiki/Op%C3%A9ration_Serval" class="mw-redirect" title="OpÃ©ration Serval">OpÃ©ration Serval</a> in January 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> A month later, Malian and French forces recaptured most of the north. <a href="/wiki/Malian_presidential_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Malian presidential election, 2013">Presidential elections</a> were held on 28 July 2013, with a second-round run-off held on 11 August, and <a href="/wiki/Malian_parliamentary_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Malian parliamentary election, 2013">legislative elections</a> were held on 24 November and 15 December 2013. </p>
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%E2%80%99etat" class="mw-redirect" title="Coup dâetat">coup dâetat</a> is currently taking place in Mali. On <a href="/wiki/2020_Malian_mutiny" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 Malian mutiny">18 August 2020</a>, the nation's president and prime minister were arrested by the military following a mutiny spurred by protests over continuing economic woes and a worsening national security situation, and the following day both resigned. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name <i>Mali</i> is taken from the&nbsp;name of the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a>. The name means "the place where the king lives"<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and carries a connotation of strength.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Guinean writer <a href="/wiki/Djibril_Tamsir_Niane" title="Djibril Tamsir Niane">Djibril Niane</a> suggests in <i>Sundiata: An Epic of Old Mali</i> (1965) that it is not impossible that Mali was the name given to one of the capitals of the emperors. 14th-century Moroccan traveler <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Battuta" title="Ibn Battuta">Ibn Battuta</a> reported that the capital of the Mali Empire was called Mali.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> One <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">Mandinka</a> tradition tells that the legendary first emperor <a href="/wiki/Sundiata_Keita" title="Sundiata Keita">Sundiata Keita</a> changed himself into a hippopotamus upon his death in the <a href="/wiki/Sankarani_River" title="Sankarani River">Sankarani River</a> and that it's possible to find villages in the area of this river, termed "old Mali", which have Mali for a name. A study of Malian proverbs noted that in old Mali, there is a village called Malikoma, which means "New Mali", and that <i>Mali</i> could have formerly been the name of a city.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Another theory suggests that <i>Mali</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fulani</a> pronunciation of the name of the <a href="/wiki/Mand%C3%A9_peoples" title="MandÃ© peoples">Mande peoples</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> It is suggested that a sound shift led to the change, whereby in Fulani the alveolar segment <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/nd/</span> shifts to <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/l/</span> and the terminal vowel denasalises and raises, leading "Manden" to shift to <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/mali/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MALI_empire_map.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/MALI_empire_map.PNG/220px-MALI_empire_map.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/MALI_empire_map.PNG/330px-MALI_empire_map.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/MALI_empire_map.PNG/440px-MALI_empire_map.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1580" data-file-height="994"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MALI_empire_map.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The extent of the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a>'s peak
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Timbuktu-manuscripts-astronomy-mathematics.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Timbuktu-manuscripts-astronomy-mathematics.jpg/220px-Timbuktu-manuscripts-astronomy-mathematics.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Timbuktu-manuscripts-astronomy-mathematics.jpg/330px-Timbuktu-manuscripts-astronomy-mathematics.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Timbuktu-manuscripts-astronomy-mathematics.jpg/440px-Timbuktu-manuscripts-astronomy-mathematics.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Timbuktu-manuscripts-astronomy-mathematics.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The pages above are from <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu_Manuscripts" title="Timbuktu Manuscripts">Timbuktu Manuscripts</a> written in Sudani script (a form of <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>) from the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a> showing established knowledge of astronomy and mathematics. Today there are close to a million of these manuscripts found in <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu" title="Timbuktu">Timbuktu</a> alone.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GriotsSambala.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/GriotsSambala.jpg/220px-GriotsSambala.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/GriotsSambala.jpg/330px-GriotsSambala.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/GriotsSambala.jpg/440px-GriotsSambala.jpg 2x" data-file-width="501" data-file-height="352"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GriotsSambala.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Griot" title="Griot">Griots</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sambala" class="mw-redirect" title="Sambala">Sambala</a>, king of MÃ©dina (<a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fula people</a>, Mali), 1890
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mali" title="History of Mali">History of Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Rock paintings and carvings indicate that northern Mali has been inhabited since prehistoric times when the Sahara was fertile grassland. Farming took place by 5000 BC and iron was used around 500 BC. Large settlements began to develop in 300 A.D., including <a href="/wiki/Djenne" class="mw-redirect" title="Djenne">Djenne</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Mali was once part of three famed West African empires which controlled <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">trans-Saharan trade</a> in gold, salt, <a href="/wiki/Slaves" class="mw-redirect" title="Slaves">slaves</a>, and other precious commodities majorly during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Mansa_Musa" title="Mansa Musa">Mansa Musa</a> from c. 1312 â c. 1337.<sup id="cite_ref-p1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p1-23">[23]</a></sup> These <a href="/wiki/Sahelian_kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahelian kingdom">Sahelian kingdoms</a> had neither rigid geopolitical boundaries nor rigid ethnic identities.<sup id="cite_ref-p1_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p1-23">[23]</a></sup> The earliest of these empires was the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Empire" title="Ghana Empire">Ghana Empire</a>, which was dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Soninke_people" title="Soninke people">Soninke</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Mande_languages" title="Mande languages">Mande</a>-speaking people.<sup id="cite_ref-p1_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p1-23">[23]</a></sup> The empire expanded throughout West Africa from the 8th century until 1078, when it was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Almoravids" class="mw-redirect" title="Almoravids">Almoravids</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a> later formed on the upper <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger River</a>, and reached the height of power in the 14th century.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> Under the Mali Empire, the ancient cities of <a href="/wiki/Djenn%C3%A9" title="DjennÃ©">DjennÃ©</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu" title="Timbuktu">Timbuktu</a> were centers of both trade and Islamic learning.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> The empire later declined as a result of internal intrigue, ultimately being supplanted by the <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> The Songhai people originated in current northwestern <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>. The Songhai had long been a major power in West Africa subject to the Mali Empire's rule.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the late 14th century, the Songhai gradually gained independence from the Mali Empire and expanded, ultimately subsuming the entire eastern portion of the Mali Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> The Songhai Empire's eventual collapse was largely the result of a <a href="/wiki/Saadi_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Saadi dynasty">Moroccan</a> invasion in 1591, under the command of <a href="/wiki/Judar_Pasha" title="Judar Pasha">Judar Pasha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> The fall of the Songhai Empire marked the end of the region's role as a trading crossroads.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/European_exploration_of_Africa" title="European exploration of Africa">establishment of sea routes by the European powers</a>, the trans-Saharan trade routes lost significance.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>One of the worst <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famines</a> in the region's recorded history occurred in the 18th century. According to <a href="/wiki/John_Iliffe_(historian)" title="John Iliffe (historian)">John Iliffe</a>, "The worst crises were in the 1680s, when famine extended from the Senegambian coast to the Upper Nile and 'many sold themselves for slaves, only to get a sustenance', and especially in 1738â1756, when West Africa's greatest recorded subsistence crisis, due to drought and locusts, reportedly killed half the population of <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu" title="Timbuktu">Timbuktu</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colonial_rule">French colonial rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: French colonial rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Africa._French_West_Africa._Currently_the_most_important_efforts_of_the_Office_du_Niger_are_directed_toward_the..._-_NARA_-_541637.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Africa._French_West_Africa._Currently_the_most_important_efforts_of_the_Office_du_Niger_are_directed_toward_the..._-_NARA_-_541637.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Africa._French_West_Africa._Currently_the_most_important_efforts_of_the_Office_du_Niger_are_directed_toward_the..._-_NARA_-_541637.tif.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Africa._French_West_Africa._Currently_the_most_important_efforts_of_the_Office_du_Niger_are_directed_toward_the..._-_NARA_-_541637.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Africa._French_West_Africa._Currently_the_most_important_efforts_of_the_Office_du_Niger_are_directed_toward_the..._-_NARA_-_541637.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Africa._French_West_Africa._Currently_the_most_important_efforts_of_the_Office_du_Niger_are_directed_toward_the..._-_NARA_-_541637.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Africa._French_West_Africa._Currently_the_most_important_efforts_of_the_Office_du_Niger_are_directed_toward_the..._-_NARA_-_541637.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1653" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Africa._French_West_Africa._Currently_the_most_important_efforts_of_the_Office_du_Niger_are_directed_toward_the..._-_NARA_-_541637.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cotton being processed in <a href="/wiki/Niono" title="Niono">Niono</a> into 180&nbsp;kg (400&nbsp;lb) bales for export to other parts of Africa and to France, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">â1950</span>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Mali fell under the control of France during the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> By 1905, most of the area was under firm French control as a part of <a href="/wiki/French_Sudan" title="French Sudan">French Sudan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> On 24 November 1958, French Sudan (which changed its name to the Sudanese Republic) became an autonomous republic within the <a href="/wiki/French_Community" title="French Community">French Community</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Independent_Mali_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent_Mali-26">[26]</a></sup> In January 1959, Mali and <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> united to become the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Federation" title="Mali Federation">Mali Federation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Independent_Mali_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent_Mali-26">[26]</a></sup> The Mali Federation gained independence from France on 20 June 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Senegal withdrew from the federation in August 1960, which allowed the Sudanese Republic to become the independent Republic of Mali on 22 September 1960, and that date is now the country's <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_independence_days" title="List of national independence days">Independence Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Modibo_Ke%C3%AFta" title="Modibo KeÃ¯ta">Modibo KeÃ¯ta</a> was elected the first president.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> KeÃ¯ta quickly established a one-party state, adopted an independent African and socialist orientation with close ties to the East, and implemented extensive nationalization of economic resources.<sup id="cite_ref-p2_24-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1960, the population of Mali was reported to be about 4.1&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Moussa_Traor.C3.A9"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Moussa_TraorÃ©">Moussa TraorÃ©</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Moussa TraorÃ©">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 19 November 1968, following progressive economic decline, the KeÃ¯ta regime was overthrown in a bloodless military coup led by <a href="/wiki/Moussa_Traor%C3%A9" title="Moussa TraorÃ©">Moussa TraorÃ©</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-p3_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-29">[29]</a></sup> a day which is now commemorated as <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Day" title="Liberation Day">Liberation Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The subsequent military-led regime, with TraorÃ© as president, attempted to reform the economy. His efforts were frustrated by political turmoil and a devastating <a href="/wiki/Sahel_drought" title="Sahel drought">drought</a> between 1968 and 1974,<sup id="cite_ref-p3_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-29">[29]</a></sup> in which famine killed thousands of people.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The TraorÃ© regime faced student unrest beginning in the late 1970s and three coup attempts. The TraorÃ© regime repressed all dissenters until the late 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-p3_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government continued to attempt economic reforms, and the populace became increasingly dissatisfied.<sup id="cite_ref-p3_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-29">[29]</a></sup> In response to growing demands for multi-party democracy, the TraorÃ© regime allowed some limited political liberalization. They refused to usher in a full-fledged democratic system.<sup id="cite_ref-p3_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-29">[29]</a></sup> In 1990, cohesive opposition movements began to emerge, and was complicated by the turbulent rise of ethnic violence in the north following the return of many <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuaregs</a> to Mali.<sup id="cite_ref-p3_29-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-29">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Place_de_la_libert%C3%A9_-_Bamako.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Place_de_la_libert%C3%A9_-_Bamako.jpg/220px-Place_de_la_libert%C3%A9_-_Bamako.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Place_de_la_libert%C3%A9_-_Bamako.jpg/330px-Place_de_la_libert%C3%A9_-_Bamako.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Place_de_la_libert%C3%A9_-_Bamako.jpg/440px-Place_de_la_libert%C3%A9_-_Bamako.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Place_de_la_libert%C3%A9_-_Bamako.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>WWI Commemorative Monument to the "ArmÃ©e Noire"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Anti-government protests in 1991 led to a coup, a transitional government, and a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mali" title="Constitution of Mali">new constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p3_29-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-29">[29]</a></sup> Opposition to the corrupt and dictatorial regime of General Moussa TraorÃ© grew during the 1980s. During this time strict programs, imposed to satisfy demands of the International Monetary Fund, brought increased hardship upon the country's population, while elites close to the government supposedly lived in growing wealth. Peaceful student protests in January 1991 were brutally suppressed, with mass arrests and torture of leaders and participants.<sup id="cite_ref-nonviolent_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nonviolent-32">[32]</a></sup> Scattered acts of rioting and vandalism of public buildings followed, but most actions by the dissidents remained nonviolent.<sup id="cite_ref-nonviolent_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nonviolent-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="March_Revolution">March Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: March Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>From 22 March through 26 March 1991, mass pro-democracy rallies and a nationwide strike was held in both urban and rural communities, which became known as <i>les Ã©venements</i> ("the events") or the March Revolution. In Bamako, in response to mass demonstrations organized by university students and later joined by trade unionists and others, soldiers opened fire indiscriminately on the nonviolent demonstrators. Riots broke out briefly following the shootings. Barricades as well as roadblocks were erected and TraorÃ© declared a state of emergency and imposed a nightly curfew. Despite an estimated loss of 300 lives over the course of four days, nonviolent protesters continued to return to Bamako each day demanding the resignation of the dictatorial president and the implementation of democratic policies.<sup id="cite_ref-nesbitt_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nesbitt-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>26 March 1991 is the day that marks the clash between military soldiers and peaceful demonstrating students which climaxed in the massacre of dozens under the orders of then President Moussa TraorÃ©. He and three associates were later tried and convicted and received the death sentence for their part in the decision-making of that day. Nowadays, the day is a national holiday in order to remember the tragic events and the people that were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (July 2013)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> The coup is remembered as Mali's March Revolution of 1991. </p>
      <p>By 26 March, the growing refusal of soldiers to fire into the largely nonviolent protesting crowds turned into a full-scale tumult, and resulted in thousands of soldiers putting down their arms and joining the pro-democracy movement. That afternoon, Lieutenant Colonel <a href="/wiki/Amadou_Toumani_Tour%C3%A9" title="Amadou Toumani TourÃ©">Amadou Toumani TourÃ©</a> announced on the radio that he had arrested the dictatorial president, Moussa TraorÃ©. As a consequence, opposition parties were legalized and a national congress of civil and political groups met to draft a new democratic constitution to be approved by a national referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-nesbitt_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nesbitt-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Amadou_Toumani_Tour.C3.A9_presidency"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Amadou_Toumani_TourÃ©_presidency">Amadou Toumani TourÃ© presidency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Amadou Toumani TourÃ© presidency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 1992, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Oumar_Konar%C3%A9" title="Alpha Oumar KonarÃ©">Alpha Oumar KonarÃ©</a> won Mali's first democratic, multi-party presidential election, before being re-elected for a second term in 1997, which was the last allowed under the constitution. In 2002 <a href="/wiki/Amadou_Toumani_Tour%C3%A9" title="Amadou Toumani TourÃ©">Amadou Toumani TourÃ©</a>, a retired general who had been the leader of the military aspect of the 1991 democratic uprising, was elected.<sup id="cite_ref-p4_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p4-35">[35]</a></sup> During this democratic period Mali was regarded as one of the most politically and socially stable countries in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_modern_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavery in modern Africa">Slavery</a> persists in Mali today with as many as 200,000 people held in direct servitude to a master.<sup id="cite_ref-slaves_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slaves-37">[37]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_Rebellion_(2012)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuareg Rebellion (2012)">Tuareg Rebellion of 2012</a>, ex-slaves were a vulnerable population with reports of some slaves being recaptured by their former masters.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Mali_conflict">Northern Mali conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Northern Mali conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mali_War" title="Mali War">Mali War</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Le_Mali_confront%C3%A9_aux_sanctions_et_%C3%A0_lavanc%C3%A9e_des_rebelles_islamistes_(6904946068).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Le_Mali_confront%C3%A9_aux_sanctions_et_%C3%A0_lavanc%C3%A9e_des_rebelles_islamistes_%286904946068%29.jpg/220px-Le_Mali_confront%C3%A9_aux_sanctions_et_%C3%A0_lavanc%C3%A9e_des_rebelles_islamistes_%286904946068%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Le_Mali_confront%C3%A9_aux_sanctions_et_%C3%A0_lavanc%C3%A9e_des_rebelles_islamistes_%286904946068%29.jpg/330px-Le_Mali_confront%C3%A9_aux_sanctions_et_%C3%A0_lavanc%C3%A9e_des_rebelles_islamistes_%286904946068%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Le_Mali_confront%C3%A9_aux_sanctions_et_%C3%A0_lavanc%C3%A9e_des_rebelles_islamistes_%286904946068%29.jpg/440px-Le_Mali_confront%C3%A9_aux_sanctions_et_%C3%A0_lavanc%C3%A9e_des_rebelles_islamistes_%286904946068%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Le_Mali_confront%C3%A9_aux_sanctions_et_%C3%A0_lavanc%C3%A9e_des_rebelles_islamistes_(6904946068).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tuareg separatist rebels in Mali, January 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In January 2012 <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_rebellion_(2012)" title="Tuareg rebellion (2012)">a Tuareg rebellion</a> began in Northern Mali, led by the <a href="/wiki/National_Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Azawad" title="National Movement for the Liberation of Azawad">National Movement for the Liberation of Azawad</a> (MNLA).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> In March, military officer <a href="/wiki/Amadou_Sanogo" title="Amadou Sanogo">Amadou Sanogo</a> seized power in <a href="/wiki/2012_Malian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2012 Malian coup d'Ã©tat">a coup d'Ã©tat</a>, citing TourÃ©'s failures in quelling the rebellion, and leading to sanctions and an embargo by the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The MNLA quickly took control of the north, declaring independence as <a href="/wiki/Azawad" title="Azawad">Azawad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> However, Islamist groups including <a href="/wiki/Ansar_Dine" title="Ansar Dine">Ansar Dine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda_in_the_Islamic_Maghreb" title="Al-Qaeda in the Islamic Maghreb">Al-Qaeda in the Islamic Maghreb (AQIM)</a>, who had helped the MNLA defeat the government, turned on the Tuareg and took control of the North<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> with the goal of implementing <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">sharia</a> in Mali.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 11 January 2013, the <a href="/wiki/French_Armed_Forces" title="French Armed Forces">French Armed Forces</a> <a href="/wiki/Operation_Serval" title="Operation Serval">intervened</a> at the request of the interim government. On 30 January, the coordinated advance of the French and Malian troops claimed to have retaken the last remaining Islamist stronghold of Kidal, which was also the last of three northern provincial capitals.<sup id="cite_ref-kidal_retaken_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kidal_retaken-45">[45]</a></sup> On 2 February, the French President, <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande" title="FranÃ§ois Hollande">FranÃ§ois Hollande</a>, joined Mali's interim President, <a href="/wiki/Dioncounda_Traor%C3%A9" title="Dioncounda TraorÃ©">Dioncounda TraorÃ©</a>, in a public appearance in recently recaptured Timbuktu.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Hollande_Timbuktu_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Hollande_Timbuktu-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflict_in_Central_Mali">Conflict in Central Mali</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Conflict in Central Mali">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the central Mali province of <a href="/wiki/Mopti_Region" title="Mopti Region">Mopti</a>, conflict has escalated since 2015 between agricultural communities like the <a href="/wiki/Dogon_people" title="Dogon people">Dogon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bambara_people" title="Bambara people">Bambara</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pastoralism" title="Pastoralism">pastoral</a> <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fula (or Fulani) people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-48">[48]</a></sup> Historically, the two sides have fought over access to land and water, factors which have been exacerbated by <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> as the Fula move into new areas.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The Dogon and the Bambara communities have formed militias, or "self-defense groups",<sup id="cite_ref-:4_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-48">[48]</a></sup> to fight the Fula. They accuse the Fula of working with armed <a href="/wiki/Islamic_terrorism" title="Islamic terrorism">Islamists</a> linked to <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-48">[48]</a></sup> While some Fula have joined Islamist groups, <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> reports that the links have been "exaggerated and instrumentalized by different actors for opportunistic ends".<sup id="cite_ref-:4_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-48">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> Added a top Mali military commander:</p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>âIâve discussed the growing violence with my commanders and with village chiefs from all sides. Yes, sure, there are jihadists in this zone, but the real problem is banditry, animal theft, score settling â people are enriching themselves using the fight against terrorists as a cover.â<sup id="cite_ref-:4_48-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>The conflict has seen the creation and growth of Dogon and Bambara militias. The government of Mali is suspected of supporting some of these groups under the guise of they being proxies in the war against Islamists in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mali_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Mali conflict">Northern Mali conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-50">[50]</a></sup> The government denies this.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-50">[50]</a></sup> One such militia is the Dogon group <a href="/wiki/Dan_Na_Ambassagou" title="Dan Na Ambassagou">Dan Na Ambassagou</a>, created in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_48-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-48">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2018, the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Humanitarian_Dialogue" title="Centre for Humanitarian Dialogue">Centre for Humanitarian Dialogue</a> negotiated a unilateral ceasefire with Dan Na Ambassagou "in the context of the conflict which opposes the group to other community armed groups in central Mali".<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> However, the group has been blamed for the <a href="/wiki/March_2019_attacks_against_Fulani_herders" class="mw-redirect" title="March 2019 attacks against Fulani herders">24 March 2019 massacre of 160 Fula villagers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The group denied the attack, but afterwards Malian President Keita ordered the group to disband.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UN Special Adviser on the Prevention of Genocide, <a href="/wiki/Adama_Dieng" title="Adama Dieng">Adama Dieng</a>, warned of a growing <a href="/wiki/Ethnicization" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnicization">ethnicization</a> of the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The United Nations reported that the number of children killed in the conflict in the first six months of 2019 was twice as many for the entire year of 2018. Many of the children have been killed in intercommunal attacks attributed to ethnic militias, with the majority of attacks occurring around <a href="/wiki/Mopti" title="Mopti">Mopti</a>. It is reported that around 900 schools have closed down and that armed militias are recruiting children.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the first week of October 2019, two jihadist attacks in the towns of Boulikessi and <a href="/wiki/Mondoro" title="Mondoro">Mondoro</a> killed more than 25 Mali soldiers near the border with <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The Malian President <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Boubacar_Ke%C3%AFta" title="Ibrahim Boubacar KeÃ¯ta">Ibrahim Boubacar KeÃ¯ta</a> declared that "no military coup will prevail in Mali", continuing that he doesn't think it "is on the agenda at all and cannot worry us".<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 19 August 2020, President KeÃ¯ta announced his resignation and the dissolution of Parliament and the Government, just hours after he was <a href="/wiki/2020_Malian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 Malian coup d'Ã©tat attempt">arrested by the insurgent military</a> following protests over corruption, economic woes, and a worsening national security situation.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_elections">2018 elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2018 elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>See <i><a href="/wiki/2018_Malian_presidential_election" title="2018 Malian presidential election">2018 Malian presidential election</a></i> </p>
      <p>Presidential elections were held in Mali on 29 July 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> In July 2018, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Constitutional_Court_of_Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Constitutional Court of Mali (page does not exist)">Constitutional Court</a> approved the nomination of a total of 24 candidates in the election.<sup id="cite_ref-africanews_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africanews-61">[61]</a></sup> As no candidate received more than 50% of the vote in the first round, a runoff was held on 12 August 2018 between the top two candidates, incumbent President <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Boubacar_Ke%C3%AFta" title="Ibrahim Boubacar KeÃ¯ta">Ibrahim Boubacar KeÃ¯ta</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Rally_for_Mali" title="Rally for Mali">Rally for Mali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Souma%C3%AFla_Ciss%C3%A9" title="SoumaÃ¯la CissÃ©">SoumaÃ¯la CissÃ©</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Union_for_the_Republic_and_Democracy" title="Union for the Republic and Democracy">Union for the Republic and Democracy</a>. KeÃ¯ta was subsequently re-elected with 67% of the vote. </p> 
      <h3><span id="2020_Coup_d.27etat"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020_Coup_d'etat">2020 Coup d'etat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2020 Coup d'etat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/2020_Malian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2020 Malian coup d'Ã©tat">2020 Malian coup d'Ã©tat</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Comit%C3%A9_national_pour_le_salut_du_Peuple_-_2020_Malian_coup_d%27Etat_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Comit%C3%A9_national_pour_le_salut_du_Peuple_-_2020_Malian_coup_d%27Etat_2.jpg/220px-Comit%C3%A9_national_pour_le_salut_du_Peuple_-_2020_Malian_coup_d%27Etat_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Comit%C3%A9_national_pour_le_salut_du_Peuple_-_2020_Malian_coup_d%27Etat_2.jpg/330px-Comit%C3%A9_national_pour_le_salut_du_Peuple_-_2020_Malian_coup_d%27Etat_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Comit%C3%A9_national_pour_le_salut_du_Peuple_-_2020_Malian_coup_d%27Etat_2.jpg/440px-Comit%C3%A9_national_pour_le_salut_du_Peuple_-_2020_Malian_coup_d%27Etat_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="540"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Comit%C3%A9_national_pour_le_salut_du_Peuple_-_2020_Malian_coup_d%27Etat_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Committee_for_the_Salvation_of_the_People" class="mw-redirect" title="National Committee for the Salvation of the People">National Committee for the Salvation of the People</a>, directory of the ruling junta in Mali
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Popular unrest began on 5 June 2020 following irregularities in the March and April parliamentary elections, including the arrest of opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Soumaila_Ciss%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Soumaila CissÃ©">Soumaila CissÃ©</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Between 11 and 23 deaths followed protests that took place from 10 to 13 June.<sup id="cite_ref-cnews_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnews-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Members of the military led by Colonel <a href="/wiki/Assimi_Go%C3%AFta" title="Assimi GoÃ¯ta">Assimi GoÃ¯ta</a> and Colonel-Major <a href="/wiki/Isma%C3%ABl_Wagu%C3%A9" title="IsmaÃ«l WaguÃ©">IsmaÃ«l WaguÃ©</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kati,_Mali" title="Kati, Mali">Kati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koulikoro_Region" title="Koulikoro Region">Koulikoro Region</a> began a mutiny on 18 August 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-cnews_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnews-63">[63]</a></sup> President Ibrahim Boubacar KeÃ¯ta, and Prime Minister Boubou CissÃ© were arrested, and shortly after midnight KeÃ¯ta announced his resignation, saying he did not want to see any bloodshed.<sup id="cite_ref-cnews_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnews-63">[63]</a></sup> WaguÃ© announced the formation of the National Committee for the Salvation of the People (CNSP) and promised elections in the future. A curfew was begun and the streets of Bamako were quiet.<sup id="cite_ref-cnews_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnews-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS) condemned the coup and demanded the reinstallation of President KeÃ¯ta.<sup id="cite_ref-neighbours_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neighbours-64">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Mali" title="Geography of Mali">Geography of Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Mali is a landlocked country in West Africa, located southwest of <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/10th_parallel_north" title="10th parallel north">10Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/25th_parallel_north" title="25th parallel north">25Â°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/13th_meridian_west" title="13th meridian west">13Â°W</a> and <a href="/wiki/5th_meridian_east" title="5th meridian east">5Â°E</a>. Mali borders <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> to <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Mali_border" title="AlgeriaâMali border">the north-northeast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mali%E2%80%93Niger_border" title="MaliâNiger border">the east</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a> to <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso%E2%80%93Mali_border" title="Burkina FasoâMali border">the south-east</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast%E2%80%93Mali_border" title="Ivory CoastâMali border">the south</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> to <a href="/wiki/Guinea%E2%80%93Mali_border" title="GuineaâMali border">the south-west</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mali%E2%80%93Senegal_border" title="MaliâSenegal border">the west</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mali%E2%80%93Mauritania_border" title="MaliâMauritania border">the north-west</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At 1,242,248 square kilometres (479,635&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), Mali is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area">24th-largest country</a> and is comparable in size to South Africa or <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>. Most of the country lies in the southern <a href="/wiki/Sahara_Desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahara Desert">Sahara Desert</a>, which produces an extremely hot, dust-laden <a href="/wiki/Sudan_(region)" title="Sudan (region)">Sudanian savanna</a> zone.<sup id="cite_ref-geography_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geography-66">[66]</a></sup> Mali is mostly flat, rising to rolling northern plains covered by <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sand</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Adrar_des_Ifoghas" title="Adrar des Ifoghas">Adrar des Ifoghas</a> massif lies in the northeast. </p>
      <p>Mali lies in the <a href="/wiki/Geographical_zone#Torrid_Zone" title="Geographical zone">torrid zone</a> and is among the hottest countries in the world. The <a href="/wiki/Thermal_equator" title="Thermal equator">thermal equator</a>, which matches the hottest spots year-round on the planet based on the mean daily annual temperature, crosses the country.<sup id="cite_ref-geography_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geography-66">[66]</a></sup> Most of Mali receives negligible rainfall and droughts are very frequent.<sup id="cite_ref-geography_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geography-66">[66]</a></sup> Late April to early October is the rainy season in the southernmost area. During this time, flooding of the Niger River is common, creating the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Niger_Delta" title="Inner Niger Delta">Inner Niger Delta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-geography_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geography-66">[66]</a></sup> The vast northern desert part of Mali has a <a href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot desert climate">hot desert climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="KÃ¶ppen climate classification">KÃ¶ppen climate classification</a> <i>BWh</i>) with long, extremely hot summers and scarce rainfall which decreases northwards. The central area has a <a href="/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot semi-arid climate">hot semi-arid climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="KÃ¶ppen climate classification">KÃ¶ppen climate classification</a> <i>BSh</i>) with very high temperatures year-round, a long, intense dry season and a brief, irregular rainy season. The southern areas have a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wet_and_dry_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical wet and dry climate">tropical wet and dry climate</a>. (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="KÃ¶ppen climate classification">KÃ¶ppen climate classification</a> <i>Aw</i>) In review, Mali's climate is tropical, with March to May being the hot, dry season. June to October is rainy, humid and mild. November to February is the cool, dry season. </p>
      <p>Mali has considerable natural resources, with gold, uranium, <a href="/wiki/Phosphates" class="mw-redirect" title="Phosphates">phosphates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaolinite" title="Kaolinite">kaolinite</a>, salt and <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> being most widely exploited. Mali is estimated to have in excess of 17,400 tonnes of uranium (measured + indicated + inferred).<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In 2012, a further uranium mineralized north zone was identified.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Mali faces numerous environmental challenges, including <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soil_erosion" title="Soil erosion">soil erosion</a>, and inadequate <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">supplies</a> of <a href="/wiki/Potable_water" class="mw-redirect" title="Potable water">potable water</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-geography_66-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geography-66">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Five terrestrial ecoregions lie within Mali's borders: <a href="/wiki/Sahelian_Acacia_savanna" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahelian Acacia savanna">Sahelian Acacia savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Sudanian_savanna" title="West Sudanian savanna">West Sudanian savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inner_Niger_Delta_flooded_savanna" class="mw-redirect" title="Inner Niger Delta flooded savanna">Inner Niger Delta flooded savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Saharan_steppe_and_woodlands" title="South Saharan steppe and woodlands">South Saharan steppe and woodlands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Saharan_montane_xeric_woodlands" title="West Saharan montane xeric woodlands">West Saharan montane xeric woodlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-70">[70]</a></sup> The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.16/10, ranking it 51<sup>st</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-71">[71]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:right;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions_and_cercles">Regions and cercles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Regions and cercles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Mali" title="Regions of Mali">Regions of Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cercles_of_Mali" title="Cercles of Mali">Cercles of Mali</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Mali" title="Communes of Mali">Communes of Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="floatright">
       <div class="noresize" style="height: 355px; width: 360px; ">
        <map name="ImageMap_1c9fd35f5b5256f2"><area href="/wiki/Tombouctou_Region" shape="rect" coords="139,113,239,150" alt="Tombouctou Region" title="Tombouctou Region"><area href="/wiki/Kidal_Region" shape="rect" coords="264,110,309,141" alt="Kidal Region" title="Kidal Region"><area href="/wiki/Gao_Region" shape="rect" coords="268,176,308,204" alt="Gao Region" title="Gao Region"><area href="/wiki/Mopti_Region" shape="rect" coords="164,220,219,247" alt="Mopti Region" title="Mopti Region"><area href="/wiki/Koulikoro_Region" shape="rect" coords="69,176,147,203" alt="Koulikoro Region" title="Koulikoro Region"><area href="/wiki/Kayes_Region" shape="rect" coords="10,232,67,264" alt="Kayes Region" title="Kayes Region"><area href="/wiki/Bamako" shape="rect" coords="6,301,75,329" alt="Bamako" title="Bamako"><area href="/wiki/Bamako" shape="rect" coords="88,277,100,289" alt="Bamako" title="Bamako"><area href="/wiki/Sikasso" shape="rect" coords="89,305,150,329" alt="Sikasso" title="Sikasso"><area href="/wiki/S%C3%A9gou_Region" shape="rect" coords="121,257,179,281" alt="SÃ©gou Region" title="SÃ©gou Region"></map>

      </div> 
      <p>Since 2016, Mali has been divided into ten regions and the District of Bamako.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Each region has a governor.<sup id="cite_ref-pictures_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pictures-73">[73]</a></sup> The implementation of the two newest regions, TaoudÃ©nit (formerly part of Tombouctou Region) and MÃ©naka (formerly <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9naka_Cercle" title="MÃ©naka Cercle">MÃ©naka Cercle</a> in Gao Region), has been ongoing since January 2016;<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-malijet_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malijet-75">[75]</a></sup> a governor and transitional council has been appointed for both regions.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The ten regions in turn are subdivided into 56 <a href="/wiki/Cercle_(Mali)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cercle (Mali)"><i>cercle</i>s</a> and 703 <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Mali" title="Communes of Mali"><i>communes</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Mali" title="Regions of Mali"><i>rÃ©gions</i></a> and Capital District are: </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extent_of_central_government_control">Extent of central government control</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Extent of central government control">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In March 2012, the Malian government lost control over Tombouctou, Gao and Kidal Regions and the north-eastern portion of Mopti Region. On 6 April 2012, the <a href="/wiki/National_Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Azawad" title="National Movement for the Liberation of Azawad">National Movement for the Liberation of Azawad</a> unilaterally declared their secession from Mali as <a href="/wiki/Azawad" title="Azawad">Azawad</a>, an act that neither Mali nor the international community <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition" title="Diplomatic recognition">recognised</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The government later regained control over these areas. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Mali" title="Politics of Mali">Politics of Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dioncounda_Traore_photo_officielle_de_campagne_3_Mali_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Dioncounda_Traore_photo_officielle_de_campagne_3_Mali_2012.jpg/220px-Dioncounda_Traore_photo_officielle_de_campagne_3_Mali_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Dioncounda_Traore_photo_officielle_de_campagne_3_Mali_2012.jpg/330px-Dioncounda_Traore_photo_officielle_de_campagne_3_Mali_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Dioncounda_Traore_photo_officielle_de_campagne_3_Mali_2012.jpg/440px-Dioncounda_Traore_photo_officielle_de_campagne_3_Mali_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3168" data-file-height="4752"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dioncounda_Traore_photo_officielle_de_campagne_3_Mali_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ex-Malian Transition President <a href="/wiki/Dioncounda_Traor%C3%A9" title="Dioncounda TraorÃ©">Dioncounda TraorÃ©</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Mali.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Flag_of_Mali.jpg/220px-Flag_of_Mali.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="320" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Flag_of_Mali.jpg/330px-Flag_of_Mali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Flag_of_Mali.jpg/440px-Flag_of_Mali.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1181" data-file-height="1716"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Mali.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Flag of Mali
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Until the military coup of 22 March 2012<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> and a second military coup in December 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Mali was a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitutional democracy">constitutional democracy</a> governed by the Constitution of 12 January 1992, which was amended in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-p14_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p14-81">[81]</a></sup> The constitution provides for a separation of powers among the executive, <a href="/wiki/Legislative" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative">legislative</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Judicial" class="mw-redirect" title="Judicial">judicial</a> branches of government.<sup id="cite_ref-p14_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p14-81">[81]</a></sup> The system of government can be described as "semi-presidential".<sup id="cite_ref-p14_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p14-81">[81]</a></sup> Executive power is vested in a president, who is elected to a five-year term by <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> and is limited to two terms.<sup id="cite_ref-p14_81-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p14-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The president serves as a <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief of state">chief of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commander_in_chief" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander in chief">commander in chief</a> of the armed forces.<sup id="cite_ref-p14_81-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p14-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> A prime minister appointed by the president serves as head of government and in turn appoints the Council of Ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-p14_81-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p14-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The unicameral National Assembly is Mali's sole legislative body, consisting of deputies elected to five-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-p15_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p15-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Following the 2007 elections, the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_Democracy_and_Progress_(Mali)" title="Alliance for Democracy and Progress (Mali)">Alliance for Democracy and Progress</a> held 113 of 160 seats in the assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The assembly holds two regular sessions each year, during which it debates and votes on legislation that has been submitted by a member or by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-p15_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p15-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mali's constitution provides for an independent judiciary,<sup id="cite_ref-p15_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p15-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> but the executive continues to exercise influence over the judiciary by virtue of power to appoint judges and oversee both judicial functions and law enforcement.<sup id="cite_ref-p15_85-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p15-85">[85]</a></sup> Mali's highest courts are the Supreme Court, which has both judicial and administrative powers, and a separate Constitutional Court that provides judicial review of legislative acts and serves as an election arbiter.<sup id="cite_ref-p15_85-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p15-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Various lower courts exist, though village chiefs and elders resolve most local disputes in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-p15_85-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p15-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Mali" title="Foreign relations of Mali">Foreign relations of Mali</a>
      </div>
