       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Mali's foreign policy orientation has become increasingly pragmatic and pro-Western over time.<sup id="cite_ref-p17_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p17-91">[91]</a></sup> Since the institution of a democratic form of government in 2002, Mali's relations with the West in general and <a href="/wiki/Mali-United_States_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Mali-United States relations">with the United States</a> in particular have improved significantly.<sup id="cite_ref-p17_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p17-91">[91]</a></sup> Mali has a longstanding yet ambivalent relationship with France, a <a href="/wiki/French_Sudan" title="French Sudan">former colonial ruler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p17_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p17-91">[91]</a></sup> Mali was active in regional organizations such as the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> until its suspension over the <a href="/wiki/2012_Malian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2012 Malian coup d'Ã©tat">2012 Malian coup d'Ã©tat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p17_91-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p17-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Working to control and resolve regional conflicts, such as in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%E2%80%99Ivoire" class="mw-redirect" title="CÃ´te dâIvoire">CÃ´te dâIvoire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, is one of Mali's major foreign policy goals.<sup id="cite_ref-p17_91-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p17-91">[91]</a></sup> Mali feels threatened by the potential for the spillover of conflicts in neighboring states, and relations with those neighbors are often uneasy.<sup id="cite_ref-p17_91-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p17-91">[91]</a></sup> General insecurity along borders in the north, including cross-border <a href="/wiki/Banditry" title="Banditry">banditry</a> and terrorism, remain troubling issues in regional relations.<sup id="cite_ref-p17_91-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p17-91">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In early 2019, <a href="/wiki/Al_Qaeda" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Qaeda">Al Qaeda</a> claimed responsibility for an attack on a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> base in Mali that killed 10 peacekeepers from <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>. 25 people were reported to have been injured in the attack. Al Qaeda's stated reason for the attack was Chad's re-establishing diplomatic ties with <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. The base was attacked in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguelhok&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Anguelhok (page does not exist)">Anguelhok</a>, a village located in an especially unstable region of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-p17_91-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p17-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Mali" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Mali">Military of Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Military_of_Mali" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Mali">Mali's military forces</a> consist of an army, which includes land forces and air force,<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-94">[94]</a></sup> as well as the paramilitary Gendarmerie and Republican Guard, all of which are under the control of Mali's Ministry of Defense and Veterans, <a href="/wiki/Civilian_control_of_the_military" title="Civilian control of the military">headed by a civilian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ns_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ns-95">[95]</a></sup> The military is underpaid, poorly equipped, and in need of rationalization.<sup id="cite_ref-ns_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ns-95">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Mali" title="Economy of Mali">Economy of Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Djenne_market.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Djenne_market.jpg/220px-Djenne_market.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Djenne_market.jpg/330px-Djenne_market.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Djenne_market.jpg/440px-Djenne_market.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3132" data-file-height="1924"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Djenne_market.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A market scene in <a href="/wiki/Djenn%C3%A9" title="DjennÃ©">DjennÃ©</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kalabougou_potters_(6392346).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Kalabougou_potters_%286392346%29.jpg/220px-Kalabougou_potters_%286392346%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="314" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Kalabougou_potters_%286392346%29.jpg/330px-Kalabougou_potters_%286392346%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Kalabougou_potters_%286392346%29.jpg/440px-Kalabougou_potters_%286392346%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1826" data-file-height="2603"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kalabougou_potters_(6392346).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kalabougou" title="Kalabougou">Kalabougou</a> potters
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Usine_de_coton_CMDT.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Usine_de_coton_CMDT.png/220px-Usine_de_coton_CMDT.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Usine_de_coton_CMDT.png/330px-Usine_de_coton_CMDT.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Usine_de_coton_CMDT.png/440px-Usine_de_coton_CMDT.png 2x" data-file-width="566" data-file-height="377"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Usine_de_coton_CMDT.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cotton processing at CMDT
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_West_African_States" title="Central Bank of West African States">Central Bank of West African States</a> handles the financial affairs of Mali and additional members of the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a>. Mali is considered one of the poorest countries in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-94">[94]</a></sup> The average worker's annual salary is approximately US$1,500.<sup id="cite_ref-state_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mali underwent economic reform, beginning in 1988 by signing agreements with the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-state_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-96">[96]</a></sup> During 1988 to 1996, Mali's government largely reformed public enterprises. Since the agreement, sixteen enterprises were privatized, 12 partially privatized, and 20 liquidated.<sup id="cite_ref-state_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-96">[96]</a></sup> In 2005, the Malian government conceded a railroad company to the Savage Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-state_96-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-96">[96]</a></sup> Two major companies, SocietÃ© de Telecommunications du Mali (<a href="/wiki/SOTELMA" class="mw-redirect" title="SOTELMA">SOTELMA</a>) and the Cotton Ginning Company (<a href="/wiki/Compagnie_malienne_pour_le_d%C3%A9veloppement_du_textile" title="Compagnie malienne pour le dÃ©veloppement du textile">CMDT</a>), were expected to be privatized in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-state_96-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between 1992 and 1995, Mali implemented an economic adjustment programme that resulted in economic growth and a reduction in financial imbalances. The programme increased social and economic conditions, and led to Mali joining the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> on 31 May 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mali is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">OHADA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ohada.com_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-98">[98]</a></sup> The gross domestic product (GDP) has risen since. In 2002, the GDP amounted to US$3.4&nbsp;billion,<sup id="cite_ref-p9_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p9-99">[99]</a></sup> and increased to US$5.8&nbsp;billion in 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-state_96-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-96">[96]</a></sup> which amounts to an approximately 17.6% annual growth rate. </p>
      <p>Mali is a part of the "Franc Zone" (<i>Zone Franc</i>), which means that it uses the <a href="/wiki/CFA_franc" title="CFA franc">CFA franc</a>. Mali is connected with the French government by agreement since 1962 (creation of <a href="/wiki/BCEAO" class="mw-redirect" title="BCEAO">BCEAO</a>). Today all seven countries of BCEAO (including Mali) are connected to French Central Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Mali's key industry is agriculture. Cotton is the country's largest crop export and is exported west throughout Senegal and CÃ´te dâIvoire.<sup id="cite_ref-Goldenhope_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldenhope-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-marshall_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marshall-102">[102]</a></sup> During 2002, 620,000 tons of cotton were produced in Mali but cotton prices declined significantly in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-Goldenhope_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldenhope-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-marshall_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marshall-102">[102]</a></sup> In addition to cotton, Mali produces rice, <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, vegetables, tobacco, and tree crops. Gold, livestock and agriculture amount to 80% of Mali's exports.<sup id="cite_ref-state_96-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Eighty percent of Malian workers are employed in agriculture. 15% of Malian workers are employed in the service sector.<sup id="cite_ref-marshall_102-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marshall-102">[102]</a></sup> Seasonal variations lead to regular <a href="/wiki/Temporary_employment" class="mw-redirect" title="Temporary employment">temporary unemployment</a> of agricultural workers.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 1991, with the assistance of the <a href="/wiki/International_Development_Association" title="International Development Association">International Development Association</a>, Mali relaxed the enforcement of mining codes which led to renewed foreign interest and investment in the mining industry.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Gold is mined in the southern region and Mali has the third highest gold production in Africa (after South Africa and <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Goldenhope_101-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldenhope-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The emergence of gold as Mali's leading export product since 1999 has helped mitigate some of the negative impact of the cotton and Ivory Coast crises.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Other natural resources include <a href="/wiki/Kaolin" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaolin">kaolin</a>, salt, <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-state_96-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-96">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_power_stations_in_Mali" title="List of power stations in Mali">List of power stations in Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Electricity and water are maintained by the Energie du Mali, or EDM, and textiles are generated by Industry Textile du Mali, or ITEMA.<sup id="cite_ref-state_96-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-96">[96]</a></sup> Mali has made efficient use of <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a>, consisting of over half of Mali's electrical power. In 2002, 700 <a href="/wiki/KWh#Multiples" class="mw-redirect" title="KWh">GWh</a> of hydroelectric power were produced in Mali.<sup id="cite_ref-marshall_102-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marshall-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Energie du Mali is an electric company that provides electricity to Mali citizens. Only 55% of the population in cities have access to EDM.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mali is endowed with renewable energy resources and according to the index of geopolitical gains and losses after energy transition (GeGaLo Index) it can gain significant benefits from the global transition to renewable energy. It is ranked no. 11 among 156 nations in the GeGaLo Index.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_infrastructure">Transport infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transport infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Mali" title="Transport in Mali">Transport in Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In Mali, there is a railway that connects to bordering countries. There are also approximately 29 airports of which 8 have paved runways. Urban areas are known for their large quantity of green and white <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">taxicabs</a>. A significant sum of the population is dependent on <a href="/wiki/Public_transportation" class="mw-redirect" title="Public transportation">public transportation</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mali_-_Bozo_girl_in_Bamako.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Mali_-_Bozo_girl_in_Bamako.jpg/170px-Mali_-_Bozo_girl_in_Bamako.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Mali_-_Bozo_girl_in_Bamako.jpg/255px-Mali_-_Bozo_girl_in_Bamako.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Mali_-_Bozo_girl_in_Bamako.jpg/340px-Mali_-_Bozo_girl_in_Bamako.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2336" data-file-height="3504"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mali_-_Bozo_girl_in_Bamako.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Bozo_people" title="Bozo people">Bozo</a> girl in Bamako
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Mali" title="Demographics of Mali">Demographics of Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population in Mali<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-9">[9]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr>

         <td style="text-align:right;">19.1 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>In 2018, Mali's population was an estimated 19.1&nbsp;million<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-9">[9]</a></sup>. The population is predominantly rural (68% in 2002), and 5%â10% of Malians are <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p6_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p6-108">[108]</a></sup> More than 90% of the population lives in the southern part of the country, especially in <a href="/wiki/Bamako" title="Bamako">Bamako</a>, which has over 1&nbsp;million residents.<sup id="cite_ref-p6_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p6-108">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2007, about 48% of Malians were younger than 12 years old, 49% were 15â64 years old, and 3% were 65 and older.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-94">[94]</a></sup> The median age was 15.9 years.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_94-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-94">[94]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> in 2014 is 45.53 births per 1,000, and the <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (in 2012) was 6.4 children per woman.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_94-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Death_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Death rate">death rate</a> in 2007 was 16.5 deaths per 1,000.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_94-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-94">[94]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth was 53.06 years total (51.43 for males and 54.73 for females).<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_94-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-94">[94]</a></sup> Mali has one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_infant_mortality_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by infant mortality rate">world's highest rates</a> of <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-p6_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p6-108">[108]</a></sup> with 106 deaths per 1,000 live births in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_94-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-94">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities_in_Mali">Largest cities in Mali</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Largest cities in Mali">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mali1974-151_hg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Mali1974-151_hg.jpg/220px-Mali1974-151_hg.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Mali1974-151_hg.jpg/330px-Mali1974-151_hg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Mali1974-151_hg.jpg/440px-Mali1974-151_hg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3982" data-file-height="2668"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mali1974-151_hg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuareg</a> are historic, nomadic inhabitants of northern Mali.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Mali's population encompasses a number of <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-Saharan">sub-Saharan</a> ethnic groups. The <a href="/wiki/Bambara_people" title="Bambara people">Bambara</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bambara_language" title="Bambara language">Bambara</a>: <i lang="bm">Bamanankaw</i>) are by far the largest single ethnic group, making up 36.5% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-p6_108-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p6-108">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Collectively, the Bambara, <a href="/wiki/Soninke_people" title="Soninke people">SoninkÃ©</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khassonk%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="KhassonkÃ©">KhassonkÃ©</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">MalinkÃ©</a> (also called <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_language" title="Mandinka language">Mandinka</a>), all part of the broader <a href="/wiki/Mand%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="MandÃ©">MandÃ©</a> group, constitute 50% of Mali's population.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_94-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-94">[94]</a></sup> Other significant groups are the <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fula</a> (French: <i lang="fr">Peul</i>; <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula</a>: <i lang="ff-Latn">FulÉe</i>) (17%), <a href="/wiki/Gur_languages" title="Gur languages">Voltaic</a> (12%), <a href="/wiki/Songhai_people" title="Songhai people">Songhai</a> (6%), and <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuareg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moor</a> (10%).<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_94-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-94">[94]</a></sup> In Mali as well as <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>, the Moors are also known as <a href="/wiki/Azawagh_Arabs" title="Azawagh Arabs">Azawagh Arabs</a>, named after the <a href="/wiki/Azawagh" title="Azawagh">Azawagh</a> region of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>. They speak mainly <a href="/wiki/Hassaniya_Arabic" title="Hassaniya Arabic">Hassaniya Arabic</a> which is one of the regional <a href="/wiki/Varieties_of_Arabic" title="Varieties of Arabic">varieties of Arabic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Personal names reflect Mali's complex regional identities.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the far north, there is a division between <a href="/wiki/Berber_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber people">Berber</a>-descended <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuareg</a> nomad populations and the darker-skinned Bella or <a href="/wiki/Tamasheq" class="mw-redirect" title="Tamasheq">Tamasheq</a> people, due to the historical spread of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Mali" title="Slavery in Mali">slavery</a> in the region. </p>
      <p>An estimated 800,000 people in Mali are descended from <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-slaves_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slaves-37">[37]</a></sup> Slavery in Mali has persisted for centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Arabic population kept slaves well into the 20th century, until slavery was suppressed by <a href="/wiki/French_Sudan" title="French Sudan">French authorities</a> around the mid-20th century. There still persist certain hereditary servitude relationships,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> and according to some estimates, even today approximately 200,000 Malians are still enslaved.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mixed European/African descendants of Muslims of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a>, as well some French, Irish, Italian and Portuguese origins live in Mali, they are known as the <a href="/wiki/Arma_people" title="Arma people">Arma people</a> (1% of the nation's population).<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although Mali has enjoyed a reasonably good inter-ethnic relationships based on the long history of coexistence, some hereditary servitude and bondage relationship exist, as well as ethnic tension between settled <a href="/wiki/Songhai_people" title="Songhai people">Songhai</a> and nomadic Tuaregs of the north.<sup id="cite_ref-p6_108-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p6-108">[108]</a></sup> Due to a backlash against the northern population after independence, Mali is now in a situation where both groups complain about discrimination on the part of the other group.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> This conflict also plays a role in the continuing <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mali_conflict_(2012%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Mali conflict (2012âpresent)">Northern Mali conflict</a> where there is a tension between both Tuaregs and the Malian government, and the Tuaregs and radical <a href="/wiki/Islamist" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamist">Islamists</a> who are trying to establish <a href="/wiki/Sharia_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharia law">sharia law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Mali" title="Languages of Mali">Languages of Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Mali's official language is <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and over 40 <a href="/wiki/African_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="African languages">African languages</a> also are spoken by the various ethnic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-p6_108-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p6-108">[108]</a></sup> About 80% of Mali's population can communicate in <a href="/wiki/Bambara_language" title="Bambara language">Bambara</a>, which serves as an important <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-p6_108-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p6-108">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the 2009 census, the languages spoken in Mali were <a href="/wiki/Bambara_language" title="Bambara language">Bambara</a> by 51.5%, <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula</a> by 8.3%, <a href="/wiki/Dogon_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dogon language">Dogon</a> by 6.6% <a href="/wiki/Sonink%C3%A9_language" class="mw-redirect" title="SoninkÃ© language">SoninkÃ©</a> by 5.7%, <a href="/wiki/Songhai_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Songhai language">Songhai</a> by 5.3%, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Malink%C3%A9_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MalinkÃ© language (page does not exist)">MalinkÃ©</a> by 5.2%, <a href="/wiki/Minianka_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Minianka language">Minianka</a> by 3.8%, <a href="/wiki/Tamasheq_language" title="Tamasheq language">Tamasheq</a> by 3.2%, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9noufo_language" class="mw-redirect" title="SÃ©noufo language">SÃ©noufo</a> by 2%, <a href="/wiki/Bobo_language" title="Bobo language">Bobo</a> by 1.9%, <a href="/wiki/Bozo_language" title="Bozo language">Tieyaxo Bozo</a> by 1.6%, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kassonk%C3%A9_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="KassonkÃ© language (page does not exist)">KassonkÃ©</a> by 1.1%, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maure_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maure language (page does not exist)">Maure</a> by 1%, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dafing_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dafing language (page does not exist)">Dafing</a> by 0.4%, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Samogo_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Samogo language (page does not exist)">Samogo</a> by 0.4%, <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> by 0.3%, other <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Mali" title="Languages of Mali">Malian languages</a> by 0.5%, other African languages by 0.2%, Foreign languages by 0.2%, and 0.7% didn't declare their language.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mali has 12 <a href="/wiki/National_language" title="National language">national languages</a> beside <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bambara_language" title="Bambara language">Bambara</a>, namely <a href="/wiki/Bomu_language" title="Bomu language">Bomu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bozo_language" title="Bozo language">Tieyaxo Bozo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Escarpment_Dogon" title="Escarpment Dogon">Toro So Dogon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maasina_Fulfulde" title="Maasina Fulfulde">Maasina Fulfulde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hassaniya_Arabic" title="Hassaniya Arabic">Hassaniya Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minyanka_language" title="Minyanka language">Mamara Senoufo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kita_Maninka_language" title="Kita Maninka language">Kita Maninkakan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soninke_language" title="Soninke language">Soninke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koyraboro_Senni" title="Koyraboro Senni">Koyraboro Senni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senara_language" title="Senara language">Syenara Senoufo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamasheq_language" title="Tamasheq language">Tamasheq</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kassonke_language" title="Kassonke language">Xaasongaxango</a>. Each is spoken as a first language primarily by the ethnic group with which it is associated. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Mali" title="Religion in Mali">Religion in Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5"><a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Mali" title="Religion in Mali">Religion in Mali</a><sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-122">[122]</a></sup></th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">Religion</td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">Percent</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Mali" title="Islam in Mali">Islam</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:green; width:90%; overflow: hidden;">
             â
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">90%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Christianity</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:blue; width:5%; overflow: hidden;">
             â
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">5%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_religion" title="Indigenous religion">Indigenous</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:red; width:5%; overflow: hidden;">
             â
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">5%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mosque_entrance_(6862566).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Mosque_entrance_%286862566%29.jpg/220px-Mosque_entrance_%286862566%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="341" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Mosque_entrance_%286862566%29.jpg/330px-Mosque_entrance_%286862566%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Mosque_entrance_%286862566%29.jpg/440px-Mosque_entrance_%286862566%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1813" data-file-height="2812"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mosque_entrance_(6862566).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An entrance to the Djinguereber mosque
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Islam was introduced to West Africa in the 11th century and remains the predominant religion in much of the region. An estimated 90% of Malians are <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Mali" title="Islam in Mali">Muslim</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a><sup id="cite_ref-pew_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-123">[123]</a></sup>), approximately 5% are Christian (about two-thirds <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Mali" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Mali">Roman Catholic</a> and one-third <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a>) and the remaining 5% adhere to <a href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religions" title="Traditional African religions">traditional African religions</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Dogon_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Dogon religion">Dogon religion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-122">[122]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">Atheism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">agnosticism</a> are believed to be rare among Malians, most of whom practice their religion daily.<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The constitution establishes a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a> and provides for <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a>, and the government largely respects this right.<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Islam as historically practiced in Mali has been malleable and adapted to local conditions; relations between Muslims and practitioners of minority religious faiths have generally been amicable.<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> After the 2012 imposition of <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">sharia</a> rule in northern parts of the country, however, Mali came to be listed high (number 7) in the Christian persecution index published by <a href="/wiki/Open_Doors" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Doors">Open Doors</a>, which described the persecution in the north as severe.<sup id="cite_ref-DeutscheWelle_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeutscheWelle-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OpenDoor_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OpenDoor-126">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Mali" title="Education in Mali">Education in Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lyc%C3%A9ens_kati.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Lyc%C3%A9ens_kati.jpg/220px-Lyc%C3%A9ens_kati.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Lyc%C3%A9ens_kati.jpg/330px-Lyc%C3%A9ens_kati.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Lyc%C3%A9ens_kati.jpg/440px-Lyc%C3%A9ens_kati.jpg 2x" data-file-width="566" data-file-height="424"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lyc%C3%A9ens_kati.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>High school students in <a href="/wiki/Kati" class="mw-redirect" title="Kati">Kati</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Public education in Mali is in principle provided free of charge and is compulsory for nine years between the ages of seven and sixteen.<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> The system encompasses six years of primary education beginning at age 7, followed by six years of secondary education.<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> Mali's actual primary school enrollment rate is low, in large part because families are unable to cover the cost of uniforms, books, supplies, and other fees required to attend.<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, the primary school enrollment rate was 61% (65% of males and 58% of females).<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> In the late 1990s, the secondary school enrollment rate was 15% (20% of males and 10% of females).<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> The education system is plagued by a lack of schools in rural areas, as well as shortages of teachers and materials.<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Estimates of literacy rates in Mali range from 27â30 to 46.4%, with literacy rates significantly lower among women than men.<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bamako" title="University of Bamako">University of Bamako</a>, which includes four constituent universities, is the largest university in the country and enrolls approximately 60,000 undergraduate and graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Mali" title="Health in Mali">Health in Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Mali faces numerous health challenges related to poverty, <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a>, and inadequate <a href="/wiki/Hygiene" title="Hygiene">hygiene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> Mali's health and development indicators rank among the worst in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> Life expectancy at birth is estimated to be 53.06 years in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> In 2000, 62â65% of the population was estimated to have access to safe drinking water and only 69% to sanitation services of some kind.<sup id="cite_ref-p7_124-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p7-124">[124]</a></sup> In 2001, the general government expenditures on health totaled about US$4 per capita at an average exchange rate.<sup id="cite_ref-p8_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p8-130">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Efforts have been made to improve nutrition, and reduce associated health problems, by encouraging women to make nutritious versions of local recipes. For example, the <a href="/wiki/International_Crops_Research_Institute_for_the_Semi-Arid_Tropics" title="International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics">International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics</a> (<a href="/wiki/ICRISAT" class="mw-redirect" title="ICRISAT">ICRISAT</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Aga_Khan_Foundation" title="Aga Khan Foundation">Aga Khan Foundation</a>, trained women's groups to make <i>equinut</i>, a healthy and nutritional version of the traditional recipe <i>di-dÃ¨guÃ¨</i> (comprising peanut paste, honey and millet or rice flour). The aim was to boost nutrition and livelihoods by producing a product that women could make and sell, and which would be accepted by the local community because of its local heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Village_Telly_in_Mali.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Village_Telly_in_Mali.jpg/220px-Village_Telly_in_Mali.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Village_Telly_in_Mali.jpg/330px-Village_Telly_in_Mali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Village_Telly_in_Mali.jpg/440px-Village_Telly_in_Mali.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Village_Telly_in_Mali.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Village in the <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a> region
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Medical facilities in Mali are very limited, and medicines are in short supply.<sup id="cite_ref-p8_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p8-130">[130]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Arthropod" title="Arthropod">arthropod</a>-borne diseases are prevalent in Mali, as are a number of <a href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Infectious disease">infectious diseases</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p8_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p8-130">[130]</a></sup> Mali's population also suffers from a high rate of child malnutrition and a low rate of <a href="/wiki/Immunization" title="Immunization">immunization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p8_130-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p8-130">[130]</a></sup> An estimated 1.9% of the adult and children population was afflicted with HIV/AIDS that year,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> among the lowest rates in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p8_130-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p8-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&nbsp;Dead link since January 2019">dead link</span></a></i>]</span></sup> An estimated 85%â91% of Mali's girls and women have had <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> (2006 and 2001 data).<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender_equality">Gender equality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Gender equality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2017, Mali ranked 157th out of 160 countries in the gender inequality index as reported by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> The Malian Constitution states that it protects women's rights, however many laws exist that discriminate against women.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-135">[135]</a></sup> Provisions in the laws limit women's decision-making power after marriage, in which the husband becomes superior to his wife.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-135">[135]</a></sup> Women are blamed for not maintaining the appearance of their husbands and are also blamed for the actions of their children if they misbehave, which encourages the cultural attitude that women are inferior to men.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_135-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-135">[135]</a></sup> The lack of participation of women in politics is due to the idea that politics is associated with men and that women should avoid this sector.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_135-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-135">[135]</a></sup> Girls' education is also an area in which boys dominate, since it is a better investment for the parents.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_135-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-135">[135]</a></sup> As traditional values and practices have contributed to gender inequality in Mali, conflict and lawlessness have also influenced the growing gap in gender through gender-based violence.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-136">[136]</a></sup> The unstable government of Mali has led to organizations like USAID attempting to improve the lives of the people, mainly women and girls' rights in order to re-engage the development of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-136">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_factors">Social factors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Social factors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Religion, the patriarchal social system, and <a href="/wiki/Gender-based_violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Gender-based violence">gender-based violence</a> are the social factors that shape women in Mali.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> These factors serve as the norm for gender relations, but are also the cause for inequalities and strengthen male domination within the household.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> Majority of the population is Muslim and it is reinforced that males dominate the household.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-138">[138]</a></sup> Traditional roles of men and women are emphasized in which the man is the head of the household and women have to meet the needs and demands of men.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-138">[138]</a></sup> So girls at a young age are shown and learn household activities like chores, cooking, childcare, etc. as that is the final duty of a woman to become a housewife and rear her children while the men provides for the family.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_138-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-138">[138]</a></sup> In the patriarchal social system, men are considered the authority and women are subject to obey and respect men.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> The primary roles of women are that of wife and mother, so childcare, house chores, meal preparation, and a discrete life is required of a Malian women.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> This means that women, in some cases, are subject to a double burden due to having professional and family obligations that does not apply to men.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> This inequality toward women then leads to the lack of education of girls in a household because boys are the priority and their education is necessary in comparison to the girls who will eventually marry and join their husband's family.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> Gender-based violence in Mali happens at the national and household level. At the national level, in 2012 the conflict in the Northern part of the country increased cases of kidnappings and rape toward women.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_136-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-136">[136]</a></sup> The conflict impacted gender and social system, and reduced women's access to resources, economy, and opportunities.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_136-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-136">[136]</a></sup> The areas of impact then influence the negative score of Mali in relation to gender equality.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_136-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-136">[136]</a></sup> At the household level, Malian women face gender-based violence through domestic violence, forced marriages, marital rape, and cultural practices in the family.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_135-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-135">[135]</a></sup> The Demographic Health Survey for Mali in 2013 stated that 76% of women and 54% of men believed physical harm towards women was acceptable if the women burnt food, argues back, goes out without notifying her husband, the children are not tended to or refuses sexual relations with her husband.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_136-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-136">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Area_of_opportunity">Area of opportunity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Area of opportunity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The lack of education has increased gender inequality in Mali because not many women are working outside the household are even participating in the Public Administration sector.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> After adjusting the entrance requirements and access to education, girls still have lower enrollment rates and less access to formal education.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> Drop-out rates for girls are 15% higher than that of boys because they have a higher responsibility at home and most parents refuse to allow all their children to go to school, so boys tend to become educated.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> Similarly, technical and vocational education has a lower numbers of girls participating and are inadequately distributed in the country because the training centers are focused in the urban cities.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> Finally, higher education for girls consist of short programs because early marriages prevent most girls from pursuing a longer term education program like those in science.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> Although women do not have the same access of education, in recent decades women have been entering and representing in decision-making positions in the Public Administration sector.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> Members of Parliament, 15 were women in 2010 out of 147 members.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> Recent decades show that women are slowly joining important decision-making positions which is changing the attitude and status of women in Mali, which has led to the promotion of women's right in the political sphere.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Efforts">Efforts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Efforts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Legislation at the international and national levels have been implemented over the decades to help promote women's rights in Mali.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> At the international, Mali signed the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Platform_for_Action" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing Platform for Action">Beijing Platform for Action</a> which suggest that women should participate in decision-making and the convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women which is the foundation to women's rights promotion.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> At the national level, Mali's Constitution has the Decree No. 092-073P-CTSP that claims equality to all Malian citizens and discrimination is prohibited, which has not been followed.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> The Poverty Reduction Strategy Programme (PRSP) and the Growth and Poverty Reduction Strategy Programme under the Malian Government seek to improve the well-being of the citizens, and changes to governance and gender in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> The Ministry for Advancement of Women, Children and the Family was created specifically for women and children so that their basics rights and needs get met under the law.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> Although there exists legislation and policy for gender equality the institutionalization of the National Gender Policy of Mali is necessary to support the importance of women's rights.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> Strengthening and the support of girls' and women's access to education and training is recommended to improve gender equality in Mali.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_137-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-137">[137]</a></sup> The involvement of international organizations like USAID assist Mali financially to enhance their development through the efforts of the improvement of women's rights.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_136-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-136">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Mali" title="Culture of Mali">Culture of Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Konoguel_Mosque_tower_(6439210).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Konoguel_Mosque_tower_%286439210%29.jpg/220px-Konoguel_Mosque_tower_%286439210%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="343" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Konoguel_Mosque_tower_%286439210%29.jpg/330px-Konoguel_Mosque_tower_%286439210%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Konoguel_Mosque_tower_%286439210%29.jpg/440px-Konoguel_Mosque_tower_%286439210%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1807" data-file-height="2815"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Konoguel_Mosque_tower_(6439210).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/w/index.php?title=Konoguel_Mosque&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Konoguel Mosque (page does not exist)">Konoguel Mosque</a> tower
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The varied everyday culture of Malians reflects the country's ethnic and geographic diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-p13_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p13-139">[139]</a></sup> Most Malians wear flowing, colorful robes called <a href="/wiki/Boubou_(clothing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Boubou (clothing)">boubous</a> that are typical of West Africa. Malians frequently participate in traditional festivals, dances, and ceremonies.<sup id="cite_ref-p13_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p13-139">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mali_Dogon_Dance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Mali_Dogon_Dance.jpg/220px-Mali_Dogon_Dance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Mali_Dogon_Dance.jpg/330px-Mali_Dogon_Dance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Mali_Dogon_Dance.jpg/440px-Mali_Dogon_Dance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1818" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mali_Dogon_Dance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mali Dogon Dance
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Mali" title="Music of Mali">Malian musical traditions</a> are derived from the <a href="/wiki/Griot" title="Griot">griots</a>, who are known as "Keepers of Memories".<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Malian music is diverse and has several different genres. Some famous Malian influences in music are <a href="/wiki/Kora_(instrument)" title="Kora (instrument)">kora</a> virtuoso musician <a href="/wiki/Toumani_Diabat%C3%A9" title="Toumani DiabatÃ©">Toumani DiabatÃ©</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ngoni_(instrument)" title="Ngoni (instrument)">ngoni</a> with <a href="/wiki/Bassekou_Kouyate" title="Bassekou Kouyate">Bassekou Kouyate</a> the virtuoso of the electric <a href="/wiki/Ngoni_(instrument)" title="Ngoni (instrument)">jeli ngoni</a>, the late roots and blues guitarist <a href="/wiki/Ali_Farka_Tour%C3%A9" title="Ali Farka TourÃ©">Ali Farka TourÃ©</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuareg</a> band <a href="/wiki/Tinariwen" title="Tinariwen">Tinariwen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khaira_Arby" title="Khaira Arby">Khaira Arby</a>, and several <a href="/wiki/Afro_pop_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro pop music">Afro-pop</a> artists such as <a href="/wiki/Salif_Keita" title="Salif Keita">Salif Keita</a>, the duo <a href="/wiki/Amadou_et_Mariam" class="mw-redirect" title="Amadou et Mariam">Amadou et Mariam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oumou_Sangare" class="mw-redirect" title="Oumou Sangare">Oumou Sangare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatoumata_Diawara" title="Fatoumata Diawara">Fatoumata Diawara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rokia_Traore" class="mw-redirect" title="Rokia Traore">Rokia Traore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Habib_Koit%C3%A9" title="Habib KoitÃ©">Habib KoitÃ©</a>. Dance also plays a large role in Malian culture.<sup id="cite_ref-embassy_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-embassy-141">[141]</a></sup> Dance parties are common events among friends, and traditional mask dances are performed at ceremonial events.<sup id="cite_ref-embassy_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-embassy-141">[141]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Though Mali's literature is less famous than its music,<sup id="cite_ref-p29_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p29-142">[142]</a></sup> Mali has always been one of Africa's liveliest intellectual centers.<sup id="cite_ref-p128_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p128-143">[143]</a></sup> Mali's literary tradition is passed mainly by word of mouth, with <i>jalis</i> reciting or singing histories and stories known by heart.<sup id="cite_ref-p128_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p128-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-p28_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p28-144">[144]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amadou_Hamp%C3%A2t%C3%A9_B%C3%A2" title="Amadou HampÃ¢tÃ© BÃ¢">Amadou HampÃ¢tÃ© BÃ¢</a>, Mali's best-known historian, spent much of his life writing these oral traditions down for the world to remember.<sup id="cite_ref-p28_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p28-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The best-known novel by a Malian writer is <a href="/wiki/Yambo_Ouologuem" title="Yambo Ouologuem">Yambo Ouologuem</a>'s <i>Le devoir de violence</i>, which won the 1968 <a href="/wiki/Prix_Renaudot" title="Prix Renaudot">Prix Renaudot</a> but whose legacy was marred by accusations of plagiarism.<sup id="cite_ref-p128_143-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p128-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-p28_144-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p28-144">[144]</a></sup> Other well-known Malian writers include Baba TraorÃ©, Modibo Sounkalo Keita, <a href="/wiki/Massa_Makan_Diabat%C3%A9" title="Massa Makan DiabatÃ©">Massa Makan DiabatÃ©</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moussa_Konat%C3%A9" title="Moussa KonatÃ©">Moussa KonatÃ©</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fily_Dabo_Sissoko" title="Fily Dabo Sissoko">Fily Dabo Sissoko</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p128_143-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p128-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-p28_144-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p28-144">[144]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mali_football.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Mali_football.jpg/220px-Mali_football.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Mali_football.jpg/330px-Mali_football.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Mali_football.jpg/440px-Mali_football.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1731" data-file-height="1128"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mali_football.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Malian children playing football in a <a href="/wiki/Dogon_people" title="Dogon people">Dogon</a> village
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Mali" title="Football in Mali">most popular sport in Mali</a> is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-p151_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p151-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-p55_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p55-146">[146]</a></sup> which became more prominent after Mali hosted the <a href="/wiki/2002_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="2002 African Cup of Nations">2002 African Cup of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p151_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p151-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-p320_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p320-147">[147]</a></sup> Most towns and cities have regular games;<sup id="cite_ref-p320_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p320-147">[147]</a></sup> the most popular teams nationally are <a href="/wiki/Djoliba_AC" title="Djoliba AC">Djoliba AC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stade_Malien" title="Stade Malien">Stade Malien</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Real_Bamako" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Bamako">Real Bamako</a>, all based in the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-p55_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p55-146">[146]</a></sup> Informal games are often played by youths using a bundle of rags as a ball.<sup id="cite_ref-p55_146-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p55-146">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Basketball is another major sport;<sup id="cite_ref-p55_146-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p55-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Mali_women%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Mali women's national basketball team">Mali women's national basketball team</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Hamchetou_Maiga" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamchetou Maiga">Hamchetou Maiga</a>, competed at the 2008 <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">Beijing Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lutte_Traditionnelle" title="Lutte Traditionnelle">Traditional wrestling</a> (<i>la lutte</i>) is also somewhat common, though popularity has declined in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-p320_147-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p320-147">[147]</a></sup> The game <a href="/wiki/Oware" title="Oware">wari</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Mancala" title="Mancala">mancala</a> variant, is a common pastime.<sup id="cite_ref-p55_146-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p55-146">[146]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Malian_cuisine" title="Malian cuisine">Malian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Malian_Tea2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Malian_Tea2.JPG/220px-Malian_Tea2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Malian_Tea2.JPG/330px-Malian_Tea2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Malian_Tea2.JPG/440px-Malian_Tea2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Malian_Tea2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Malian tea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Rice and <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a> are the staples of <a href="/wiki/Malian_cuisine" title="Malian cuisine">Malian cuisine</a>, which is heavily based on cereal grains.<sup id="cite_ref-p30_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p30-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-p146_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p146-151">[151]</a></sup> Grains are generally prepared with sauces made from edible leaves, such as <a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">spinach</a> or <a href="/wiki/Adansonia_digitata" title="Adansonia digitata">baobab</a>, with tomato peanut sauce, and may be accompanied by pieces of grilled meat (typically chicken, <a href="/wiki/Mutton" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutton">mutton</a>, beef, or goat).<sup id="cite_ref-p30_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p30-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-p146_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p146-151">[151]</a></sup> Malian cuisine varies regionally.<sup id="cite_ref-p30_150-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p30-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-p146_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p146-151">[151]</a></sup> Other popular dishes include <a href="/wiki/Fufu" title="Fufu">fufu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jollof_rice" title="Jollof rice">jollof rice</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maafe" class="mw-redirect" title="Maafe">maafe</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Mali" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Mali">Media of Mali</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In Mali, there are several newspapers such as <i><a href="/wiki/Les_%C3%89chos_(Mali)" class="mw-redirect" title="Les Ãchos (Mali)">Les Echos</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/L%27Essor" title="L'Essor">L'Essor</a></i>, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Info_Matin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Info Matin (page does not exist)">Info Matin</a></i>, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nouvel_Horizon_(Mali)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nouvel Horizon (Mali) (page does not exist)">Nouvel Horizon</a></i>, and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Le_R%C3%A9publicain_(Mali)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Le RÃ©publicain (Mali) (page does not exist)">Le RÃ©publicain</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Le_R%C3%A9publicain_(Mali)" class="extiw" title="fr:Le RÃ©publicain (Mali)">fr</a>]</span></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Mali" title="Telecommunications in Mali">Telecommunications in Mali</a> include 869,600 mobile phones, 45,000 televisions and 414,985 Internet users.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mali&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
